<div id="review_202492781" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202492781" />
    <a title="Leonor (Ner)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3648579-leonor-ner"><img alt="Leonor (Ner)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444328674p2/3648579.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202492781?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leonor (Ner)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leonor (Ner)" href="/user/show/3648579-leonor-ner">Leonor (Ner)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Harry Potter fans and those who are ardently wishing a good continuation of the saga,</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Leonor (Ner) by: </span>
      Eduardo Serra
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3648579-leonor-ner?shelf=harry-potter">harry-potter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3648579-leonor-ner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3648579-leonor-ner?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3648579-leonor-ner?shelf=j-k-rowling">j-k-rowling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer202492781&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202492781" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16509172467723777529">Also published in <a href='http://cupofcoffeeandabook.blogspot.pt/2012/07/review-james-potter-and-hall-of-elders.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>"A Cup of Coffee and a Book"</a><br/><br/>I am not giving this 4 stars just because this isn't J.K. Rowling's official work.<br/><br/>This was a very pleasant reading. Normally I'm sceptical about fan-fictions concerning a saga I absolutely worship. However, this was recommended to me by another "Harry Potter" fan so I've decided to give it a go. Also, the idea of having some sort of continuation after "Deathly Hallows", made me grab this story and read it, forgetting it wasn't written by the genius h</span>
  <span id="freeText16509172467723777529" style="display:none">Also published in <a href="http://cupofcoffeeandabook.blogspot.pt/2012/07/review-james-potter-and-hall-of-elders.html" rel="nofollow noopener">"A Cup of Coffee and a Book"</a><br /><br />I am not giving this 4 stars just because this isn't J.K. Rowling's official work.<br /><br />This was a very pleasant reading. Normally I'm sceptical about fan-fictions concerning a saga I absolutely worship. However, this was recommended to me by another "Harry Potter" fan so I've decided to give it a go. Also, the idea of having some sort of continuation after "Deathly Hallows", made me grab this story and read it, forgetting it wasn't written by the genius herself.<br /><br />This "book" - since it's not a true publication but an on-line reading - manages to create a plausible continuation for Harry Potter saga, this time being his son James the main character. It's a Potter, still. The characters were created in a way that resembled the previous characters, being Ted Lupin my ultimate favourite one. That particular character reminded me of the Weasley twins, which was amazing since I kind of miss them. Ralph and Zane were a mixture of Ron/Hermione/Luna and Neville, in my opinion, bringing the same comic relief as them and the true bond of friendship. As for James, to me he was a new version of his father, perhaps a little bit more mature than his father in his first year. Of course that having Harry Potter as your dad helps you viewing the world differently. Cedric surprised me since I was not expecting him to be a ghost wandering Hogwarts, completely lost and speechless. I admire the fact he was kind of connected with Snape in helping James and his friends. And I also thought about him as the new Gryffindor ghost, forgetting as James that he wasn't a Gryffindor at all.<br /><br />The idea of the American delegation was very well explored. I admit never having thought of that while reading Rowling's work, but Lippert managed to pick something completely different from what we were excepting, and transform it into a plausible (sorry the repetition of words) plot that would make us - my opinion of course - forget that we are not reading Rowling. Also, the Merlin plot was one of the reason it caught my attention. One great wizard as Merlin coming back from the "dead" and ruling was something I just needed to know how it would end. Truth be told that I never expected Merlin to be considered as the new Headmaster.<br /><br />The writing was extremely well planned and carefully written. There were moments I forgot, as I've mentioned, that I wasn't reading J.K. Rowling since the author really did tried his best to keep as faithful as he could to the original writing. Even the jokes sounded as something the genius herself could write. For that, good work.<br /><br />Overall, I think this was a very well written story based on Harry Potter, a pleasant reading that, not being official, will definitely fill your imagination as a possible continuation of the saga.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16509172467723777529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Harry Potter fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer325121179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14986758991041643134">I'm torn between 3 or 4 stars for this book (again!). It was definitely well written, and had a very similar tone and voice as the original Harry Potter series. The characters and the happenings all felt genuine. But there were a few scenes I just didn't take to - some new creatures and magical practices didn't <i>quite</i> feel at home in Rowling's universe, and some scenes were very talky and harder to get through so that I felt like reading was a chore at times. I was able to predict a lot of things</span>
  <span id="freeText14986758991041643134" style="display:none">I'm torn between 3 or 4 stars for this book (again!). It was definitely well written, and had a very similar tone and voice as the original Harry Potter series. The characters and the happenings all felt genuine. But there were a few scenes I just didn't take to - some new creatures and magical practices didn't <i>quite</i> feel at home in Rowling's universe, and some scenes were very talky and harder to get through so that I felt like reading was a chore at times. I was able to predict a lot of things that happened toward the end of the story way beforehand, although one thing did catch me off guard and it was really cool. But, predictability always knocks off a point for me. However, I do think this story is worth a shot for any Harry Potter fan, and I will continue reading this series by Lippert. He did it very well, and it was great to be back in the world of Harry Potter! Also, to the author's credit any time I started to question if something he wrote about was accurate to HP canon, it was then explained.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16536366312878818780">Most fan fiction is unreadable crap, but there are a few authors who can actually write at a professional level, or nearly so. If you like Harry Potter and the very idea of fan fiction doesn't make you turn up your nose, then this next generation story is worth reading. While I didn't like all of the elements Lippert added into the "canon" universe (the Americans and the "quantum" explanation of magic, for instance), it's otherwise very much in the same spirit as the original books.</span>

<div id="review_208667693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208667693" />
    <a title="Gabbo Parra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5729824-gabbo-parra"><img alt="Gabbo Parra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499985518p2/5729824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208667693?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabbo Parra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabbo Parra" href="/user/show/5729824-gabbo-parra">Gabbo Parra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer208667693&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208667693" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15625728188931080219">I have to admit this book surprised me, and it did in a very good way. Not just because I didn’t know this series existed, but by how much Mr. Lippert channels J.K. Rowling. In many moments, you couldn’t distinguish between the two authors, and that is a huge accomplishment.<br/><br/>This book has the same silly moments of awkwardness that made the Harry Potter series delightful and remarkably close to the human realm and not as something mythical because of magic and supernatural and otherworldly creatur</span>
  <span id="freeText15625728188931080219" style="display:none">I have to admit this book surprised me, and it did in a very good way. Not just because I didn’t know this series existed, but by how much Mr. Lippert channels J.K. Rowling. In many moments, you couldn’t distinguish between the two authors, and that is a huge accomplishment.<br /><br />This book has the same silly moments of awkwardness that made the Harry Potter series delightful and remarkably close to the human realm and not as something mythical because of magic and supernatural and otherworldly creatures, which I think is what gave it its resounding success.<br /><br />Now I’m going to start with the spoilers. I loved the fact that the three protagonists were not only just boys, but also boys from different houses. It expanded the range of movement of the characters in a very interesting way, and at the end, it was not just to be diverse, but downright purposeful.<br /><br />I had three favorite moments. When the ghost of Cedric Diggory talked to James Potter through the inscription on the Triwizard Cup, it was an eerie moment masterfully displayed, and I give big kudos to Mr. Lippert for that.<br /><br />I loved the part of Old Mrs. Black distracted by TV. Superb touch to quiet her outbursts.<br /><br />And when Merlin gave a chunk of his staff to the son of the squib, my eyes watered. It was a most inspiring moment, and it made perfect sense.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book, not only as an extension of the Harry Potter world, but because I believe, it is a truly refreshing approach to a well-known subject.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15625728188931080219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64849098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7975528752718056805">So I ran into this online. (I think I actually saw it mentioned on GoodReads) and I am a HUGE Harry Potter dork. <br/>I started reading this and literally felt dirty for the first 20 pages, so I stopped. I felt as if I was betraying Rowling. However, I looked this book up on wiki and apparently Rowling tried to stop the production of this and then talked with the author and gave her blessing as long as it is promoted as fan fic. But that's wiki..who knows if that is true. <br/>So I picked up where I left </span>
  <span id="freeText7975528752718056805" style="display:none">So I ran into this online. (I think I actually saw it mentioned on GoodReads) and I am a HUGE Harry Potter dork. <br />I started reading this and literally felt dirty for the first 20 pages, so I stopped. I felt as if I was betraying Rowling. However, I looked this book up on wiki and apparently Rowling tried to stop the production of this and then talked with the author and gave her blessing as long as it is promoted as fan fic. But that's wiki..who knows if that is true. <br />So I picked up where I left off once I felt I had the blessing of the most high author in the world. <br />This book was not Rowling's work or even close to it. However, the image of Harry and Ginny's kid going to Hogwarts was fantastic! I love Teddy Lupin and hearing about him, Victorie, and other characters from my favorite series made this worth the read. <br />It's a free download (I guess the author can't legally make money on this?) and it's worth the time to read it. It's an easy read and a way to get back and enjoy the world we probably all love!<br />I'm going to only give this 4 stars though. Out of loyalty to Rowling.</span>

<div id="review_690137762" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/690137762" />
    <a title="Kitty Red-Eye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15490662-kitty-red-eye"><img alt="Kitty Red-Eye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367176432p2/15490662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/690137762?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kitty Red-Eye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kitty Red-Eye" href="/user/show/15490662-kitty-red-eye">Kitty Red-Eye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15490662-kitty-red-eye?shelf=entertainment">entertainment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15490662-kitty-red-eye?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15490662-kitty-red-eye?shelf=fantasy-or-scifi">fantasy-or-scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer690137762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7783497228462287667">This book was both an easy and a difficult read: at times I wanted to stop reading and at times I found it good. I was as big a Harry Potter fan as anyone, but I never read fanfic before, because I just didn't think it felt right, I didn't want to get my "journey" messed up with many different fictional universes - many with dubious quality, to put it nicely. <br/><br/>So this was my first fanfic experience. I'm in a very foreign country, learning a very foreign language and reading about complicated and </span>
  <span id="freeText7783497228462287667" style="display:none">This book was both an easy and a difficult read: at times I wanted to stop reading and at times I found it good. I was as big a Harry Potter fan as anyone, but I never read fanfic before, because I just didn't think it felt right, I didn't want to get my "journey" messed up with many different fictional universes - many with dubious quality, to put it nicely. <br /><br />So this was my first fanfic experience. I'm in a very foreign country, learning a very foreign language and reading about complicated and war-ridden history and politics, and yesterday I really needed a break from all the psycho-ness of reality. <i>James Potter and the Hall of Elders' Crossing</i> provided that much-needed break, and I am grateful for it. I knew I had to let go of J.K. Rowling's Hogwarts and dive into someone else's Hogwarts, which was a little difficult, I admit, but ok - either you do it, or you just don't read the book. I liked going back to Hogwarts, even if this Hogwarts was a different one, with different characters (also the "old" characters like McGonnagall, Snape-in-portrait and even Harry himself were different characters, since they're written by another author), different storytelling, different style. It's ok. I found James' struggle with standing in his fathers' shadow a funny parallell to author Lippert's actual situation - no matter how well (or not) he writes, he will be in author Rowling's shadow. And as James Potter thinks, that he must be a <i>different</i> kind of hero from his father, Lippert must be a <i>different</i> sort of Hogwarts creator from Rowling. Maybe this wasn't intentional, but it was impossible to not think of it. <br /><br />All in all: If you can let Rowling's Hogwarts go and just dive into another person's Hogwarts, there will be no problem with reading this book, it'll be just like any other book, some will like it and some will not. After all, even if Hogwarts and the Potterverse is the creation and property of Rowling, the idea of the Potterverse belongs to everyone who has ever visited. That a place and a fictional universe can be re-visited by others, I think is ultimately a very good thing. Don't expect it to be like the original, because it will never be. <br /><br />All in all, I found it interesting to experience fanfic. While reading, I wondered why the author kept writing something he would have to publish for free - writing a book is a lot of work, and rarely pays off, but here, it'll be impossible for all future to make as much as a dime off it - instead of developing his own fictional universe that he can actually make some money from. At the end, I saw that he has done that too. I hope he'll have luck with that. It is *really* a lot of work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7783497228462287667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_646932717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646932717" />
    <a title="Sarah Stevens" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1335564-sarah-stevens"><img alt="Sarah Stevens" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219370387p2/1335564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646932717?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Stevens" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Stevens" href="/user/show/1335564-sarah-stevens">Sarah Stevens</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646932717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14558293529906068801">When I saw this book in eReads for my iPhone, I was really pleased. I thought it would be great to indulge in my love for the wizarding world with a fresh set of stories, especially since the ratings weren't half bad.<br/><br/>But just a few pages in and I couldn't believe how awful it was. I couldn't even make it through until the end of the second chapter, and I almost always finish a book once I've started. <br/><br/>First off are just the blatant incongruencies. I mean, if you are going to do a Potter continuat</span>
  <span id="freeText14558293529906068801" style="display:none">When I saw this book in eReads for my iPhone, I was really pleased. I thought it would be great to indulge in my love for the wizarding world with a fresh set of stories, especially since the ratings weren't half bad.<br /><br />But just a few pages in and I couldn't believe how awful it was. I couldn't even make it through until the end of the second chapter, and I almost always finish a book once I've started. <br /><br />First off are just the blatant incongruencies. I mean, if you are going to do a Potter continuation, you have to at least make it consistent with the way the world has already been painted. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mundungus Fletcher tall? House elves showing their faces in the Great Hall? Any first years allowed on the Quidditch team? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It was almost like the author had read the originals a long time ago and didn't bother refreshing his memory before writing these. <br /><br />Secondly, there are a lot of new things he added that just didn't fit. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mean, what equipment shed is going to be within walking distance of Hogwarts and the Quidditch pitch and still need protection from Muggles? And students impersonating aliens? Really? And why would they let an American who is only in the country for a year attend? It's not like he couldn't go back to America for school - it is a boarding school after all. Hogwarts may have exchange students, but not transfer students. And it is a little ridiculous that Harry Potter's son would be so woefully uneducated about Muggle life. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Finally, the writing just falls flat in general. You barely get a sense for where things are set and who is involved. I think it must be that the author relies too heavily on readers' prior knowledge of the wizarding world and so he doesn't bother setting up people or places properly, so everything seems rather disengaged. For example, a floating door opens up into a cave. But can you actually picture that without a door frame to define the edges of the portal? I can't. But the author figures hey, it's magic so I can do what I want and you'll have to believe it. Either that or he didn't think it through. I don't know which is worse. <br /><br />The only reason I didn't give it one star is for little moments of character touches that I found charming, like James when he gets sorted. Overall though, reading this almost makes me want to try to write a story for James Potter just to get the bad taste of this story out of my mouth. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14558293529906068801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4597939468525350235">I gave this 5 stars instead of 4 purely out of my enjoyment of the book not necessarily the quality of writing. The tone of it definitely stays true to Rowling, her books, and the characters. I believe the author is just like the rest of us fans who are a little sad that we have no more Harry Potter books or movies to look forward to. So he gave us what we needed. And I gulped it down nonetheless. As I first started reading it, I was surprised that I was a little teary-eyed and emotional. It rea</span>
  <span id="freeText4597939468525350235" style="display:none">I gave this 5 stars instead of 4 purely out of my enjoyment of the book not necessarily the quality of writing. The tone of it definitely stays true to Rowling, her books, and the characters. I believe the author is just like the rest of us fans who are a little sad that we have no more Harry Potter books or movies to look forward to. So he gave us what we needed. And I gulped it down nonetheless. As I first started reading it, I was surprised that I was a little teary-eyed and emotional. It really was almost like sending my own kid to school. I grew up with Harry, Hermione, and Ron. And now fast forward and they have school-age children. <br /><br />Overall, it was a good story, creative and true to the Potter-verse. Interesting new characters as well as the favorites we all know and love. I will be reading the other two installments as well. <br /><br />The things that I noticed-being a picky reader. If I am right, the author is American. There is quite a few Americanisms in the book and you notice it more in the dialogue. Not necessarily a bad thing but that was the reminder to me that this was not a true Rowling novel.But as I said, overall it was a good story and a nice continuation for those of us who miss Harry Potter.</span>

<div id="review_61049088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61049088" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61049088?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

          marked it as abandoned




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61049088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15078533752553946149">I didn't get very far in this book. I don't really read fan-fiction, in general, but heard so much hype about this, and it was a free download, so I thought I'd give it a chance. But I couldn't get into it.<br/><br/>One thing I liked is that Muggle-borns actually talk about growing up in the Muggle world, and things like video games and computers existing. <br/><br/>But there were a lot of weird little incongruities that kept bugging me. In relation to the thing I just mentioned, yes, it's all well and good to talk</span>
  <span id="freeText15078533752553946149" style="display:none">I didn't get very far in this book. I don't really read fan-fiction, in general, but heard so much hype about this, and it was a free download, so I thought I'd give it a chance. But I couldn't get into it.<br /><br />One thing I liked is that Muggle-borns actually talk about growing up in the Muggle world, and things like video games and computers existing. <br /><br />But there were a lot of weird little incongruities that kept bugging me. In relation to the thing I just mentioned, yes, it's all well and good to talk about it, but when the Muggle-borns go on and on and on about it, it gets a bit old.<br /><br />I thought the whole Americans coming to Hogwarts was weird. I mean, it would've been fine to have them visit, but to have them teach while they were there was weird. Madam Maxine and Karkaroff didn't teach, for instance, when they were visiting for Goblet of Fire. <br /><br />I also really did not like the way Lippert tried to ground everything in science, and explain how magic is all explainable by quantum physics. While I enjoy quantum physics, I found his discussions on it boring - not to mention grounding everything in science sort of ruins a lot of the fun, whimsy and, in his hands, the point of magic.<br /><br />But I think, even worse, were the little touches that threw me off - first years and fifth years sharing not only dorm rooms, but also taking the same classes? Quidditch on a weekday?<br /><br />I suppose I would be one of the people that Lippert refers to as "the Canon Police". Well, to him I say that perhaps if his writing and characters were more engaging I could get past the jarring quality of these things, but it's not and I couldn't.<br /><br />Perhaps I shall pick this up again and give it another go. I freely admit that I didn't get very far, and the real meat of the story hasn't started yet, so maybe it gets better. But, honestly, whenever I think about going back to it, at least for now, I have no desire whatsoever. So, for now, I leave it abandoned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15078533752553946149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2789387874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2789387874" />
    <a title="Jay-Dee Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/81277445-jay-dee-davis"><img alt="Jay-Dee Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524633885p2/81277445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2789387874?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay-Dee Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay-Dee Davis" href="/user/show/81277445-jay-dee-davis">Jay-Dee Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2789387874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3432565665560802962">This is a really accomplished work of fanfiction. There were times when I almost forgot that I was reading something that was not written by Rowling. The author has done a really good job of mimicking Rowling's writing style, and overall it is a well thought out and engaging story, even though it did lose some steam in second half. However, I think being so good is also the books downfall. <br/>While I know that with fanfiction you inevitably have to deal with the author not necessarily following est</span>
  <span id="freeText3432565665560802962" style="display:none">This is a really accomplished work of fanfiction. There were times when I almost forgot that I was reading something that was not written by Rowling. The author has done a really good job of mimicking Rowling's writing style, and overall it is a well thought out and engaging story, even though it did lose some steam in second half. However, I think being so good is also the books downfall. <br />While I know that with fanfiction you inevitably have to deal with the author not necessarily following established canon (I mean, there is a fanfiction with the Hogwarts castle getting it on with the giant squid), this book is just so close to being the real deal that when it does not follow canon it is jarring and feels unnecessary and annoying. I HATED that students of different grades were in the same classes together (this does not even make sense in the real world), students spent time in the common rooms that were not of their own houses, electronics worked on Hogwarts grounds, and that Quidditch was played during the school day in the middle of the week. Don't even get me started on how certain elements of magic were being taught to students with a decidedly scientific flair (a community that has actively spurned the influence of muggle culture/knowledge for thousands of years has somehow completely changed how magic is taught in the 16 odd years since the end of HP? Really?). As a long time fanfiction reader I willing to allow for some variation from canon, but the choices the author made were in my opinion just stupid, and in some cases, the authors own laziness in wanting to use the same characters for every single scene. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3432565665560802962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YMLSxf5hPPsbVlpISu8pawTHSioPFGmsJcFnOReoTCGJ+UTrgc0cIu9pkDV+qslvzKCRSi/tAej8ghp+Zd47uA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z23kZGQ7+FJ4dtc4F5lTmrwebCpztEc2lU3ND9/Sv1gmVnJKG5fYi4xJHUUj3LOedHm3SlNNL3JMDrBIraTIwQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_53138867'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53138867-joe-foss-flying-marine?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Joe Foss Flying Marine: The Story of his Flying Circus<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/298153.Joe_Foss?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Joe Foss<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.70 avg rating &mdash; 927 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1943\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer9736887677452635225\">Joe Foss was one of the deadliest Marines to ever sit in the cockpit of a fighter aircraft.  With 26 victories to his name, he became the first pilot to equal Eddie Rickenbacker’s American World War I record.  In October 1942, Foss and his regiment w<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9736887677452635225\" style=\"display:none\">Joe Foss was one of the deadliest Marines to ever sit in the cockpit of a fighter aircraft.  With 26 victories to his name, he became the first pilot to equal Eddie Rickenbacker’s American World War I record.  In October 1942, Foss and his regiment were sent into the heat of battle at Guadalcanal.  Foss quickly gained a reputation for aggressive close-in fighter tactics and uncanny gunnery skills and rose to become the lead pilot of what was called Foss’ Flying Circus.  Foss’ book Joe Foss Flying Marine: The Story of his Flying Circus is a remarkable work that demonstrates just how tough life could be for a fighter pilot in the Pacific Theater of World War One.  Through the course of the book Foss explains how he became a pilot, despite the fact he was initially deemed too old, why he, and men like him, chose to fight the war in the air and what it was like to engage in dogfights with Japanese pilots.  “His remarkable flying skill, inspiring leadership and indomitable fighting spirit were distinctive factors in the defense of strategic American positions on Guadalcanal.” Franklin D. Roosevelt, President, United States.  Joe Foss’ citation read: “For extraordinary achievement while participating in aerial flights with Marine Fighting Squadron 121 in the Solomon Islands area. During the period Oct. 13 to Oct. 20, 1942, inclusive, Captain Foss shot down six enemy Zero fighters and one enemy bomber in aerial combat. His constant aggressiveness, skill, and leadership during these engagements were worthy of the highest traditions of the Naval Service.”  Joe Foss was a United States Marine Corps major and the leading Marine fighter ace in World War II. He received the Medal of Honor in recognition of his role in air combat during the Guadalcanal Campaign. His book Joe Foss Flying Marine: The Story of his Flying Circus was first published in 1943.
